тАЩ рд╣рд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрдХреЗрд╢реЛ рд░рдЬрд╕реЛ рд╡рд┐рд╕рд╛рд░ рдЗрддрд┐ рджреНрд╡реЗ рддреНрд╡рдВ рддреНрдпрд╛ рдЪрд┐рджрдЪреНрдпреБрддрд╛ рдзрд╛рдордиреНрддреЗ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рдВ рднреБрд╡рдирдордзрд┐ рд╢реНрд░рд┐рддрдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. реи. резрей ) рдЗрддрд┐ редред

Jamison Brereton

79
Agni
Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa
12 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh 1тАУ3, uс╣гс╣Зih 4тАУ6, g─Бyatr─л 7тАУ12
As its position in the sequence and its metrical disunity suggest, this hymn actually consists of four separate hymns of three verses each (1тАУ3, 4тАУ6, 7тАУ9, 10тАУ12). The last three are relatively simple in their construction and their contents, but the first is rich and vividly descriptive and poses some problems of interpretation.
This first hymn segment begins (vs. 1) with quick sketches of different forms of fire: fire as sun (p─Бda a); fire as lightning (p─Бda b); ritual fire, especially as it is kindled at dawn (p─Бdas cd). This verse manages to convey dynamism without the use of a single finite verb or participle. The next two verses (2тАУ3) take up the second image, fire as lightning, and develop it in unexpected ways. In our reading, the ritual fire (that is, the god Agni) is compared with and ultimately identified with the thunderstorm, and therefore its product, the fructifying rain, can be pre
sented, paradoxically, as the product of fire itself, a substance that in nature cannot produce water. In verse 2 the zigzagging lightning flashes are the fireтАЩs flames; the bellowing bull is the roaring fire itself, and the flying mists and thundering clouds are the billowing smoke. Verse 3 takes this naturalistic comparison to its logical but unnatural conclusion: if fire is the embodiment of the thunderstorm, then it is full of rain, a most desirable product, here called тАЬthe milk of truth.тАЭ In the last half of this verse the principal ─Аdityas as well as Wind become involved by engorging the clouds with water.
After this complex and allusive vignette, the other three hymn segments are a serious anticlimax. In verses 4тАУ6 Agni is asked to give wealth and fame and to protect against demons. Wealth is also the preoccupation of verses 7тАУ9. In the final three verses the poet, Gotama, exhorts himself to give hymns to Agni, and then implores Agni to keep demons away. There is nothing in these nine verses to arrest the attention, but GotamaтАЩs first three verses are indeed a worthy gift for the god.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Agni See the published introduction. for the structure of this hymn (or rather the four hymns collected here) and for an analysis of the first three verses.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe golden-haired Agni is the agitator of the clouds when the rain is poured forth, and, moving with the swiftness of the wind, shines with a bright radiance. The mornings know not (of the showers, like honest (people), who, provided with food, are intent upon their own labours.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Satyaс╕е, true, sincere; praj─Бс╕е, people or progeny is added

Jamison Brereton

A golden-haired one in his spread through the dusky realmтАФa snake, tumultuous, swooping like the windтАФ
blazing bright (when he becomes) cognizant of Dawn, like the glorious busy (Dawns themselves) actually present.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As Geldner notes, the identifications of Agni with sun (a), lightning (b), and fire (cd) are LudwigтАЩs.

Most comm. take r├бjasaс╕е as a subjective genitive with vis─Бr├й (most clearly in GeldnerтАЩs тАЬwenn der Raum sich weitet,тАЭ referring to morning in his view). I take it rather to refer to the light of the sunтАЩs rays (his golden hair) spreading through the midspace at dawn.

The third p─Бda refers to the blazing up of the ritual fire at dawn. The fourth p─Бda consists only of a simile, couched entirely in the feminine plural. The referent of these feminine adjectives and the point of comparison with Agni are both unclear.

Geldner supplies Frauen; Renou suggests waters; Oldenberg (SBE) waters or dawns. The dawns seem most likely (so also Witzel Got┼Н), since a sg. dawn already appears in c and dawns make sense in this ritual context. Dawns are called ap├бsas тАШbusyтАЩ in I.92.3, also a Gotama hymn, and Uс╣гas is y├б┼Ыasvat─л in X.11.3. If the feminines are the dawns, the point of comparison may be ┼Ы├║cibhr─Бj─Бс╕е тАШhaving bright blazingтАЩ, since the dawns are also bright. If instead it is one of the adjectives in p─Бda d (тАШgloriousтАЩ y├б┼Ыasvat─лс╕е, тАШbusyтАЩ apasy├║vaс╕е, or тАШactually presentтАЩ saty─Б╠Бс╕е), we must assume that an original masc. sg. adj. has been attracted into the fem. pl. in the simile - not a problematic assumption.

HE in mid-air’s expanse hath golden tresses; a raging serpent, like the rushing tempest:

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe falling (rays), accompanied by the moving (Maruts), strike against (the cloud); the black shedder of rain has roared; when this is done, (the shower) comes with delightful and smiling (drops), the rain descends, the clouds thunder.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your fine-feathered (lightning flashes) zigzagged along their ways. The black bull keeps bellowing. If he is really here,
he has come here with his (lightning flashes) like kindly, smiling (girls). The mists fly; the clouds thunder.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Again, the interpretation of the image in p─Бda a depends on what the referent is. Most (Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н) take suparс╣З─Б╠Б(с╕е) as referring to AgniтАЩs flames as birds. These flames transform themselves (─Б╠БтАж aminanta) into storm clouds. As indicated in the published introduction, I instead think this verse develops the image of Agni as lightning found in 1b. The suparс╣З─Б╠Бс╕е are then the lightning flashes. This entails a somewhat bold interpretation of the verb (though I would say no bolder than тАШtransform themselvesтАЩ, for which no parallels are cited), from тАШchange, exchange, alternateтАЩ to the physical image тАШzigzagтАЩ, from тАШchange/alternate back and forthтАЩ. The middle of тИЪm─л is several times used of night and dawn swapping their colors back and forth (I.96.5, 113.2), which can be conceived of as an alternating pattern like zigzags. Against the flickering light of the lightning there appears the black bull, that is, the thunder cloud, in b. The nonce perfect non─Бva, backformed to the intensive (see the repeated nonumaс╕е of the immed. preceding hymn I.78), I take as presential, with Narten (1981 тАЬVedisch lel─Б╠Бya,тАЭ p. 2 with nn. 7, 8, = KlSch. p. 234), against most comm., although no harm would come of taking it as a preterite.

The p─Бda-final tag y├бd─лm├бm is curious. It cannot be part of what precedes, since non─Бva is unaccented. The same phrase is found at IV.5.11, where I tr. тАЬif it is here.тАЭ I interpret it in the same fashion here, but in addition assume an enjambement with the following p─Бda. Others keep it within its half verse (which I would prefer), but in their interpretation the phrase seems like mere filler (e.g., GeldnerтАЩs тАЬwenn dies (so ist)тАЭ).

The smiling females of c must be the lightning flashes (so also Geldner, Renou); cf. V.52.6 vidy├║taс╕е тАж j├бjjhat─лr iva тАЬlightning flashes like giggling (girls).тАЭ Oldenberg (SBE): rain showers, Witzel Got┼Н (tentatively): dawns. The тАЬhe,тАЭ subject of ─Б╠Бg─Бt is the black bull of b, the thundercloud as roaring fire.

For the semantic connection between these parts of the thunderstorm and the aspects of fire see the published introduction.

Griffith

Thy well-winged flashes strengthen in their manner, when the black Bull hath bellowed round about us.
With drops that bless and seem to smile he cometh: the waters fall, the clouds utter their thunder.

Oldenberg

By thy goings the beautifully-winged (birds) were disparaged 1; the black bull 2 has roared, when here 3 (all this happened). He has come as if with the bounteous smiling (women) 4. The mists fly, the clouds thunder.

рдпрджреАрдВ рдпрджрд╛рдпрдордЧреНрдирд┐рдГ рдЛрддрд╕реНрдп рдЙрджрдХрд╕реНрдп рдкрдпрд╕рд╛ рдкрдпреЛрд╡рддреНрд╕рд╛рд░рднреВрддреЗрди рд░рд╕реЗрди рдкрд┐рдпрд╛рдирдГ рдЬрдЧрджрд╛рдкреНрдпрд╛рдпрдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреН рдЖрдкреНрдпрд╛рдпрд┐рддрдВ рдЪ рдЬрдЧрддреН рдЛрддрд╕реНрдп рдЙрджрдХрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рд░рдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдареИрдГ рдЛрдЬреБрддрдореИрдГ рдкрдерд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреИрдГ рд╕реНрдирд╛рдирдкрд╛рдирд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдирдпрдиреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкрдпрдиреН рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рддрджрд╛рдиреАрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдпрдорд╛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░реЛ рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ рдЪ рдкрд░рд┐рдЬреНрдорд╛ рдкрд░рд┐рддреЛ рдЧрдиреНрддрд╛ рдорд░реБрджреНрдЧрдгрд╢реНрдЪ рдЙрдкрд░рд╕реНрдп рдореЗрдШрд╕реНрдп рдпреЛрдиреМ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреБрджрдХреЛрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рддреНрд╡рдЪрдВ рдкреГрдЮреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╡реГрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпреБрджрдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЪреНрдЫрд╛рджрдХрдВ рдкреНрд░рджреЗрд╢рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдХреАрдпреИрд░рд╛рдпреБрдзреИрдГ рд╕рдВрдпреЛрдЬрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЙрджреНрдШрд╛рдЯрдпрдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН рее рдкрд┐рдпрд╛рдирдГ ред тАШ рд╕реНрдлрд╛рдпреА рдУрдкреНрдпрд╛рдпреА рд╡реГрджреНрдзреМ’ ред’ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдВ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рдкреЛ рд▓реБрдХреН ред рдзрд╛рддреЛрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдкреАрднрд╛рд╡рдГ ред рдЕрдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддреЗрддреНрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд▓рд╕рд╛рд░реНрд╡рдзрд╛рддреБрдХрд╛рдиреБрджрд╛рддреНрддрддреНрд╡реЗ рдзрд╛рддреБрд╕реНрд╡рд░рдГ рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рд░рдЬрд┐рд╖реНрдареИрдГ ред рдЛрдЬреБрд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН рдЗрд╖реНрдЯрдирд┐ тАШ рд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рд░реНрдЬреЛрд╢реНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ ’ ( рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рем. рек. резремреи ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдЛрдХрд╛рд░рд╕реНрдп рд░рддреНрд╡рдореН ред’ рдЯреЗрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЯрд┐рд▓реЛрдкрдГ ред рдкреГрдЮреНрдЪрдиреНрддрд┐ ред’ рдкреГрдЪреА рд╕рдВрдкрд░реНрдХреЗ ред рд░реМрдзрд╛рджрд┐рдХрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen this, (the lightning, Agni), nourishes the world with the milk of the rain, and conducts it by the most direct ways to (the enjoyment of) water, then Mitra, Aryaman, Varuс╣Зa and the circumambient (troop of Maruts) pierce through the (investing) membrane into the womb of the cloud.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Direct ways: uses (as drinking, washing, bathing)

Jamison Brereton

When he, swollen with the milk of truth, (has come) leading them [=the lightning flashes] along the straightest paths of truthтАФ
Aryaman, Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, and the Earth-circling (Wind) engorge the skin in the womb of the nearer (realm).

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take ab as a parallel and paraphrase of 2c, with Agni/the thunder cloud leading (n├бyan) the lightning flashes, while himself swollen with rain. Others supply different objects, and a radical (and in my view misguided) view of the passage makes n├бyan a 3rd pl. finite verb with Agni as its object - quite awkward because he is in the nominative in p─Бda a (p├нy─Бnaс╕е). Those who hold that view resolve the syntactic problem in ad hoc ways, by emendation (*p├нy─Бnaс╣Г Oldenberg [SBE], subsequently rejected in Noten) or by taking с╣Ыt├бsya p├бyas─Б p├нy─Бnaс╕е as a parenthetical (Renou).

It is unclear whether p├бrijm─Б is meant as an epithet of Varuс╣Зa or a separate entity. Arguments can be made either way: in VII.40.6 the adjective qualifies wind and is associated with rain, and having Wind (V─Бta) involved in this thunderstorm context would be understandable. On the other hand, a fourth god would break up the unity of the standard ─Аditya triad. The same p─Бda is found in X.93.4, but in the context of a longer list of gods.

Geldner, Renou take the тАЬskinтАЭ as that of the earth, but I think it is rather the clouds in the lower atmosphere. So, more or less, Oldenberg (SBE) and Witzel Got┼Н. Cf. nearby I.62.5 (attributed to a Gautama) div├│ r├бja ├║param astabh─Бyaс╕е тАЬyou propped up the nearer realm of heaven.тАЭ

Griffith

When he comes streaming with the milk of worship, conducting by directest paths of Order
Aryaman, Mitra, Varuna, Parijman fill the hide full where lies the nether press-stone.

Oldenberg

When they have led him, who swells 1 with the milk of Rita, on the straightest paths of Rita, then Aryaman, Mitra, and Varuna, he who walks round the earth 2, fill the leather-bag (the cloud) in the womb of the lower (atmosphere [?]) 3.

Geldner

Wenn er von dem rechtm├д├Яigen Nasse voll, ihn lenkend auf den rechtm├д├Яigen richtigsten Wegen kommt, so tr├дnken Aryaman, Mitra, Varuna, der umherfahrende, die Haut im Scho├Яe des unteren Raums.

Grassmann

Sobald er strotzet von der Milch des Opfers, sie f├╝hrend auf des Opfers gradsten Wegen, So f├╝llen Mitra, Varuna, Paridschman und Arjaman den Schlauch beim untern Pressstein.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe, the blazing Agni, who is wise, and the granter of dwellings, is to be praised by our hymns; oс╕е! you whose mouth (glows) with many (flames), shine (propitiously, so) that food-providing wealth may be ours.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

With many (flames); purvaс╣З─лka, from puru, many and an─лka, face or mouth; jv─Бl─Б-jihv─Б, flame-tongued is Agni

Jamison Brereton

On being kindled, Agni the good poet is to be reverently invoked with a hymn.
Shine richly for us, you of many faces.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The irregular sandhi of v├бс╣гuс╣г kav├нс╕е may be based on that in nearby vid├║с╣г kav├нс╕е in I.71.10, though the hymns are attributed to different poets. On this sandhi phenomenon in general, see comm. ad VII.18.2.

Griffith

He, Agni, kindled, good and wise, must be exalted in our song:
Shine, thou of many forms, shine radiantly on us.

Oldenberg

Being lighted, a Vasu, a sage, Agni who is to be magnified by (pious) words, O (god) with many faces, shine to us so that riches may be ours.

Geldner

Du der Gott, der Seher Agni, der mit Lobesworten anzurufen ist, w├дhrend er entz├╝ndet wird, leuchte uns reiches Gut zu, du Vielgesichtiger!

Grassmann

Der gute Seher ist entflammt, durch Lieder Agni preisenswerth, O vielgestalt’ger, strahle reiches Gut uns zu.

Elizarenkova

Through the nights in your own person, King Agni, and at the dawning of dawn,
o sharp-fanged one, burn against the demons.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take the point of the double ut├б construction (probably, with Klein DGRV 359, a nonce based on ca тАж ca) to be the contrast of the two time periods: at night Agni must burn against the demons by himself (tm├бn─Б), but when Dawn comes, her light helps him out.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAgni, who in all rites are to be praised, guard us with your protection, (propitiated) by the recitation of the metrical hymn.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Help us, Agni, with your help at the presentation of the g─Бyatr─л song, o you to be extolled in all hymnic visions.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Since this is the first verse of a hymn in G─Бyatr─л (vss. 7-9), I take g─Бyatr├бsya as a reference to a composition in that meter, rather than just a song.

On the basis of X.4.1 v├бndyo no h├бveс╣гu, I construe the loc. in c with the gerundive.

Griffith

Adorable in all our rites, favour us, Agni, with thine aid,
When the great hymn is chanted forth.

Oldenberg

Bless us, O Agni, with thy blessings, when our G├вyatra song is brought forward (to thee), thou to whom reverence is due in all our prayers.

Geldner

Hilf uns mit deinen Hilfen, o Agni, bei dem Vortrag des Gesangesliedes, bei allen frommen Gedanken, du Lobenswerter!

Grassmann

Der du bei jedem Andachtswerk zu r├╝hmen bist, o Agni, hilf Uns huldvoll bei des Liedes Sang.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬGrant us, Agni, for our livelihood, wealth, with sound understanding, conferring happiness, and sustaining (us) through life.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(Bring) here to us wealth affording lifelong prosperity with your kind attention, o Agni.
Confer grace, (for us) to live.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I supply bhara from 8a; giving the matching verse openings, ─Б╠Бno, and the same object r├бyim, this seems the correct choice (so also Geldner, Renou, Witzel Got┼Н). It would also be possible to make r├бyim here the object of dhehi (so Oldenberg [SBE]). There are no consequences either way.

Griffith

Give us, O Agni, through thy grace wealth that supporteth all our life,
Thy favour so that we may live.

Oldenberg

Bestow on us, Agni, through thy kindness 1 wealth which may last all our life 2, and have mercy 3 on us that we may live.

Geldner

Bring uns, Agni, durch dein Wohlwollen Reichtum, der lebenslang n├дhrt. Schenk uns Gnade, auf da├Я wir leben!

Grassmann

Nach deiner Huld, o Agni, gib uns Gut, das alles Leben schafft, Und Gnade schenk zum Leben uns.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬGotama, desirous of wealth, offers to the sharp-flaming Agni pure prayers and praises.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Present your own purified speeches to sharp-flamed Agni, o Gotama; present your own hymns, as you seek his favor.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The middle voice of the impv. bh├бrasva is correlated with the self-addressed of the poet. See Jamison 2007: 104; 2009 [Skjaervo Fs.], esp. p. 70, and VII.88.1.

Griffith

O Gotama, desiring bliss present thy songs composed with care
To Agni of the pointed flames.

Oldenberg

O Gotama 1, bring forward purified words, bring songs to the sharp-flaming Agni, desirous of his favour.

Auf, bringe sch├╢ne Spr├╝che nun und Lieder dem hellgl├дnzenden, Dem Agni dar, o Gotama.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay he, Agni, who annoys us, whether nigh or afar perish; and do you be to us (propitious) for our advancement.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Whoever will assail us, close by or in the distance, let him fall, o Agni. Be (ready) to strengthen only us.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The unusual post-verbal, p─Бda-final s├бс╕е is a nice match for the initial y├бс╕е that it picks up.

Griffith

May the man fall, O Agni, who near or afar assaileth us:
Do thou increase and prosper us.

Oldenberg

May he who tries to harm us, whether nigh or afar, fall down. Do thou lead us alone to increase.

Geldner

Wer uns, Agni, nah und fern bedroht, der soll zu Fall kommen. Sei uns zum Gedeihen!

Grassmann

Wer, Agni, uns zu schaden sucht nah oder fern, der sinke hin, Uns aber sei zum Heile du.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe thousand-eyed, all-beholding, Agni, drives away the r─Бkс╣гasas, and (praised by us) with holy hymns, he, the (invoker of the gods) celebrates their praise.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sahasr─Бkс╣гa = asaс╣Гkhy─Бta jv─Бl─Бс╕е, having countless flames

Jamison Brereton

Thousand-eyed, boundless Agni repels the demonic forces.
As Hotar, worthy of praise, he is hymned.

Griffith

Keen and swift Agni, thousand-eyed, chaseth the Raksasas afar:
He singeth, herald meet for lauds.

Oldenberg

The thousand-eyed Agni, who dwells among all tribes, scares away the Rakshas. The praiseworthy Hotri (Agni) is praised 1.

Geldner

Grassmann

Allwirkend, tausend├дugig wehrt die Zaubergeister Agni ab, Der hehre Priester wird ger├╝hmt.
